class="gallerytext">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Monte_Binga" title="Monte Binga">Monte Binga</a>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozambique_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Mozambique_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/220px-Mozambique_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Mozambique_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/330px-Mozambique_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Mozambique_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/440px-Mozambique_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1900" data-file-height="1900" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozambique_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mozambique map of K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification.</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Mozambique" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of Mozambique">Climate of Mozambique</a></div>\n<p>Mozambique has a tropical climate with two seasons, a wet season from October to March and a dry season from April to September. Climatic conditions, however, vary depending on altitude. Rainfall is heavy along the coast and decreases in the north and south. Annual precipitation varies from 500 to 900&#160;mm (19.7 to 35.4&#160;in) depending on the region, with an average of 590&#160;mm (23.2&#160;in). Cyclones are common during the wet season. Average temperature ranges in Maputo are from 13 to 24&#160;\xc2\xb0C (55.4 to 75.2&#160;\xc2\xb0F) in July and from 22 to 31&#160;\xc2\xb0C (71.6 to 87.8&#160;\xc2\xb0F) in February.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Mozambique" title="Wildlife of Mozambique">Wildlife of Mozambique</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Flora_of_Mozambique" title="Category:Flora of Mozambique">Category:Flora of Mozambique</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_marine_molluscs_of_Mozambique" title="List of marine molluscs of Mozambique">List of marine molluscs of Mozambique</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_non-marine_molluscs_of_Mozambique" title="List of non-marine molluscs of Mozambique">List of non-marine molluscs of Mozambique</a></div>\n<p>There are known to be <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_Mozambique" title="List of birds of Mozambique">740 bird species</a> in Mozambique, including 20 globally threatened species and two introduced species, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_mammals_of_Mozambique" title="List of mammals of Mozambique">over 200 mammal species</a> endemic to Mozambique, including the critically endangered <a href="/wiki/Selous%27_zebra" title="Selous&#39; zebra">Selous\' zebra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vincent%27s_bush_squirrel" title="Vincent&#39;s bush squirrel">Vincent\'s bush squirrel</a> and 13 other endangered or vulnerable species.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Protected_areas_of_Mozambique" title="Protected areas of Mozambique">Protected areas of Mozambique</a> include thirteen forest reserves, seven national parks, six nature reserves, three frontier conservation areas and three wildlife or game reserves.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Mozambique" title="Politics of Mozambique">Politics of Mozambique</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Filipe_Nyusi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Filipe_Nyusi.jpg/220px-Filipe_Nyusi.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Filipe_Nyusi.jpg/330px-Filipe_Nyusi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Filipe_Nyusi.jpg/440px-Filipe_Nyusi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5472" data-file-height="3648" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Filipe_Nyusi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Incumbent President <a href="/wiki/Filipe_Nyusi" title="Filipe Nyusi">Filipe Nyusi</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Conselho_Municipal_de_Maputo_frente.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Conselho_Municipal_de_Maputo_frente.jpg/220px-Conselho_Municipal_de_Maputo_frente.jpg" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Conselho_Municipal_de_Maputo_frente.jpg/330px-Conselho_Municipal_de_Maputo_frente.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Conselho_Municipal_de_Maputo_frente.jpg/440px-Conselho_Municipal_de_Maputo_frente.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1928" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Conselho_Municipal_de_Maputo_frente.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Maputo City Hall</div></div></div>\n<p>Mozambique is a multi-party democracy under the 1990 constitution. The executive branch comprises a President, <a href="/wiki/Heads_of_Government_of_Mozambique" class="mw-redirect" title="Heads of Government of Mozambique">Prime Minister</a>, and Council of Ministers. There is a <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_the_Republic_of_Mozambique" class="mw-redirect" title="Assembly of the Republic of Mozambique">National Assembly</a> and municipal assemblies. The judiciary comprises a Supreme Court and provincial, district, and municipal courts. <a href="/wiki/Suffrage" title="Suffrage">Suffrage</a> is universal at eighteen. In the 1994 <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Mozambique" title="Elections in Mozambique">elections</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joaquim_Chissano" title="Joaquim Chissano">Joaquim Chissano</a> was elected President with 53% of the vote, and a 250-member National Assembly was voted in with 129 <a href="/wiki/FRELIMO" title="FRELIMO">Liberation Front of Mozambique</a> (<a href="/wiki/FRELIMO" title="FRELIMO">FRELIMO</a>) deputies, 112 <a href="/wiki/RENAMO" title="RENAMO">Mozambican National Resistance</a> (<a href="/wiki/RENAMO" title="RENAMO">RENAMO</a>) deputies, and nine representatives of three smaller parties that formed the Democratic Union (UD). Since its formation in 1994, the National Assembly has made progress in becoming a body increasingly more independent of the executive. By 1999, more than one-half (53%) of the legislation passed originated in the Assembly.<sup id="cite_ref-BilateralRelationsFactSheet_13-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilateralRelationsFactSheet-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After some delays, in 1998 the country held its first local elections to provide for local representation and some budgetary authority at the municipal level. The principal opposition party, RENAMO, boycotted the local elections, citing flaws in the registration process. Independent slates contested the elections and won seats in municipal assemblies. Turnout was very low.<sup id="cite_ref-BilateralRelationsFactSheet_13-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilateralRelationsFactSheet-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the aftermath of the 1998 local elections, the government resolved to make more accommodations to the opposition\'s procedural concerns for the second round of multiparty national elections in 1999. Working through the National Assembly, the electoral law was rewritten and passed by consensus in December 1998. Financed largely by international donors, a very successful voter registration was conducted from July to September 1999, providing voter registration cards to 85% of the potential electorate (more than seven million voters).<sup id="cite_ref-BilateralRelationsFactSheet_13-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilateralRelationsFactSheet-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The second general elections were held 3\xe2\x80\x935 December 1999, with high <a href="/wiki/Voter_turnout" title="Voter turnout">voter turnout</a>. International and domestic observers agreed that the voting process was well organised and went smoothly. Both the opposition and observers subsequently cited flaws in the tabulation process that, had they not occurred, might have changed the outcome. In the end, however, international and domestic observers concluded that the close result of the vote reflected the will of the people.<sup id="cite_ref-BilateralRelationsFactSheet_13-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilateralRelationsFactSheet-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>President Chissano won the presidency with a margin of 4% over the RENAMO-Electoral Union coalition candidate, <a href="/wiki/Afonso_Dhlakama" title="Afonso Dhlakama">Afonso Dhlakama</a>, and began his five-year term in January 2000. <a href="/wiki/FRELIMO" title="FRELIMO">FRELIMO</a> increased its majority in the National Assembly with 133 out of 250 seats. RENAMO-UE coalition won 116 seats, one went independent, and no third parties are represented.<sup id="cite_ref-BilateralRelationsFactSheet_13-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilateralRelationsFactSheet-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The opposition coalition did not accept the National Election Commission\'s results of the presidential vote and filed a formal complaint to the Supreme Court. One month after the voting, the court dismissed the opposition\'s challenge and validated the election results. The opposition did not file a complaint about the results of the legislative vote.<sup id="cite_ref-BilateralRelationsFactSheet_13-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilateralRelationsFactSheet-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The second local elections, involving thirty-three municipalities with some 2.4&#160;million registered voters, took place in November 2003. This was the first time that FRELIMO, RENAMO-UE, and independent parties competed without significant boycotts. The 24% turnout was well above the 15% turnout in the first municipal elections. FRELIMO won twenty-eight mayoral positions and the majority in twenty-nine municipal assemblies, while RENAMO won five mayoral positions and the majority in four municipal assemblies. The voting was conducted in an orderly fashion without violent incidents. However, the period immediately after the elections was marked by objections about voter and candidate registration and vote tabulation, as well as calls for greater transparency.\n</p><p>In May 2009, the government approved a new general elections law that contained innovations based on the experience of the 2003 municipal elections. Presidential and National Assembly elections took place on 1\xe2\x80\x932 December 2004. FRELIMO candidate <a href="/wiki/Armando_Guebuza" title="Armando Guebuza">Armando Guebuza</a> won with 64% of the popular vote. His opponent, Afonso Dhlakama of RENAMO, received 32% of the popular vote. FRELIMO won 160 seats in Parliament. A coalition of RENAMO and several small parties won the 90 remaining seats. Armando Guebuza was inaugurated as the President of Mozambique on 2 February 2005.\n</p><p>RENAMO and some other opposition parties made claims of election fraud and denounced the result. These claims were supported by international observers (among others by the European Union Election Observation Mission to Mozambique and the Carter Centre) to the elections who criticised the fact that the National Electoral Commission (CNE) did not conduct fair and transparent elections. They listed a whole range of shortcomings by the electoral authorities that benefited the ruling party FRELIMO.\n</p><p>According to EU observers, the elections shortcomings have probably not affected the final result in the presidential election. On the other hand, the observers have declared that the outcome of the parliamentary election and thus the distribution of seats in the National Assembly does not reflect the will of the Mozambican people and is clearly to the disadvantage of RENAMO.\n</p><p>After clashes between RENAMO guards and the police in Muxungue and Gondola in April 2013, RENAMO said it would boycott and disrupt local elections in November 2013. Since the end of the civil war in 1992, about 300 RENAMO guards had remained armed and refused to join the national army or the police force.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Mozambique" title="Foreign relations of Mozambique">Foreign relations of Mozambique</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Embassy_of_Mozambique,_Washington,_D.C..jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Embassy_of_Mozambique%2C_Washington%2C_D.C..jpg/220px-Embassy_of_Mozambique%2C_Washington%2C_D.C..jpg" width="220" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Embassy_of_Mozambique%2C_Washington%2C_D.C..jpg/330px-Embassy_of_Mozambique%2C_Washington%2C_D.C..jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Embassy_of_Mozambique%2C_Washington%2C_D.C..jpg/440px-Embassy_of_Mozambique%2C_Washington%2C_D.C..jpg 2x" data-file-width="1625" data-file-height="1843" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Embassy_of_Mozambique,_Washington,_D.C..jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mozambique\'s embassy in Washington, D.C.</div></div></div>\n<p>While allegiances dating back to the liberation struggle remain relevant, Mozambique\'s foreign policy has become increasingly pragmatic. The twin pillars of Mozambique\'s foreign policy are maintenance of good relations with its neighbours<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> and maintenance and expansion of ties to development partners.<sup id="cite_ref-BilateralRelationsFactSheet_13-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilateralRelationsFactSheet-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the 1970s and the early 1980s, Mozambique\'s foreign policy was inextricably linked to the struggles for majority rule in <a href="/wiki/Rhodesia" title="Rhodesia">Rhodesia</a> and South Africa as well as superpower competition and the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Mozambique\'s decision to enforce UN sanctions against Rhodesia and deny that country access to the sea led <a href="/wiki/Ian_Smith" title="Ian Smith">Ian Smith</a>\'s government to undertake overt and covert actions to oppose the country. Although the change of government in Zimbabwe in 1980 removed this threat, the government of South Africa continued to destabilize Mozambique.<sup id="cite_ref-BilateralRelationsFactSheet_13-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilateralRelationsFactSheet-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Mozambique also belonged to the <a href="/wiki/Front_Line_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Front Line States">Front Line States</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The 1984 <a href="/wiki/Nkomati_Accord" title="Nkomati Accord">Nkomati Accord</a>, while failing in its goal of ending South African support to RENAMO, opened initial diplomatic contacts between the Mozambican and South African governments. This process gained momentum with South Africa\'s elimination of <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a>, which culminated in the establishment of full diplomatic relations in October 1993. While relations with neighbouring Zimbabwe, Malawi, Zambia and Tanzania show occasional strains, Mozambique\'s ties to these countries remain strong.<sup id="cite_ref-BilateralRelationsFactSheet_13-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilateralRelationsFactSheet-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the years immediately following its independence, Mozambique benefited from considerable assistance from some Western countries, notably the <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavians</a>. The Soviet Union and its allies became Mozambique\'s primary economic, military and political supporters, and its foreign policy reflected this linkage. This began to change in 1983; in 1984 Mozambique joined the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>. Western aid by the Scandinavian countries of <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> quickly replaced Soviet support.<sup id="cite_ref-BilateralRelationsFactSheet_13-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilateralRelationsFactSheet-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> are becoming increasingly important sources of development assistance. <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> also maintains a profile in Mozambique as a result of its key role during the peace process. Relations with Portugal, the former colonial power, continue to be important because Portuguese investors play a visible role in Mozambique\'s economy.<sup id="cite_ref-BilateralRelationsFactSheet_13-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilateralRelationsFactSheet-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Mozambique is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a> and ranks among the moderate members of the African bloc in the United Nations and other international organisations. Mozambique also belongs to the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> (formerly the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_African_Unity" title="Organisation of African Unity">Organisation of African Unity</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a>. In 1994, the government became a full member of the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of the Islamic Conference</a>, in part to broaden its base of international support but also to please the country\'s sizeable Muslim population. Similarly, in 1995 Mozambique joined its <a href="/wiki/Anglophone" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglophone">Anglophone</a> neighbours in the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>. At the time it was the only nation to have joined the Commonwealth that was never part of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>. In the same year, Mozambique became a founding member and the first President of the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a> (CPLP), and maintains close ties with other <a href="/wiki/Portuguese-speaking" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese-speaking">Portuguese-speaking</a> countries.<sup id="cite_ref-BilateralRelationsFactSheet_13-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilateralRelationsFactSheet-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Mozambique" title="Provinces of Mozambique">Provinces of Mozambique</a>, <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Mozambique" title="Districts of Mozambique">Districts of Mozambique</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Postos_of_Mozambique" title="Postos of Mozambique">Postos of Mozambique</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Maputo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Maputo.jpg/300px-Maputo.jpg" width="300" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Maputo.jpg/450px-Maputo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Maputo.jpg/600px-Maputo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="483" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Maputo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A panoramic view of <a href="/wiki/Maputo" title="Maputo">Maputo</a>, the capital of Mozambique and the largest city in the country. Maputo city is separate from the <a href="/wiki/Maputo_Province" title="Maputo Province">Maputo Province</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Mozambique is divided into ten provinces (<i>provincias</i>) and one capital city (<i>cidade capital</i>) with provincial status. The provinces are subdivided into 129 districts (<i>distritos</i>). The districts are further divided in 405 "Postos Administrativos" (Administrative Posts) and then into Localidades (Localities), the lowest geographical level of the central state administration. Since 1998, 53 "Munic\xc3\xadpios" (Municipalities) have been created in Mozambique.\n</p>\n<table border="0">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="vertical-align:middle;">\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Niassa_Province" title="Niassa Province">Niassa</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cabo_Delgado_Province" title="Cabo Delgado Province">Cabo Delgado</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Nampula_Province" title="Nampula Province">Nampula</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tete_Province" title="Tete Province">Tete</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Zambezia_Province" title="Zambezia Province">Zambezia</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Manica_Province" title="Manica Province">Manica</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sofala_Province" title="Sofala Province">Sofala</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Gaza_Province" title="Gaza Province">Gaza</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Inhambane_Province" title="Inhambane Province">Inhambane</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Maputo" title="Maputo">Maputo</a> (city)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Maputo_Province" title="Maputo Province">Maputo</a></li></ol>\n</td>\n<td style="width:230px; vertical-align:middle;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozambique,_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg" class="image" title="Map of Mozambique with the province highlighted"><img alt="Map of Mozambique with the province highlighted" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Mozambique%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg/170px-Mozambique%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg.png" width="170" height="256" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Mozambique%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg/255px-Mozambique%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Mozambique%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg/340px-Mozambique%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1134" data-file-height="1707" /></a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Mozambique" title="Districts of Mozambique">districts of Mozambique</a> are divided into 405 <i>postos</i>.\n</p><p><i>Postos administrativos</i> (administrative posts) are the main subdivisions of districts. This name, in use during colonial times, was abolished after independence<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> and was replaced by <i>localidades</i> (localities). However, it was re-established in 1986.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Administrative posts are headed by a <i>Secret\xc3\xa1rios</i> (secretaries), which before independence were called <i>Chefes de Posto</i> (post chiefs).\n</p><p>Administrative posts can be further subdivided into localities, also headed by secretaries.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Mozambique operates a small, functioning military that handles all aspects of domestic national defence, the <a href="/wiki/Mozambique_Defence_Armed_Forces" title="Mozambique Defence Armed Forces">Mozambique Defence Armed Forces</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Mozambique" title="Economy of Mozambique">Economy of Mozambique</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozambique_treemap.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Mozambique_treemap.png/350px-Mozambique_treemap.png" width="350" height="273" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Mozambique_treemap.png/525px-Mozambique_treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Mozambique_treemap.png/700px-Mozambique_treemap.png 2x" data-file-width="1106" data-file-height="862" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozambique_treemap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A proportional representation of Mozambique\'s exports</div></div></div>\n<p>The official currency is the <a href="/wiki/Mozambican_metical" title="Mozambican metical">New Metical</a> (as of March 2018, 1&#160;USD is roughly equivalent to 62 New Meticals), which replaced old Meticals at the rate of a thousand to one. The old currency was redeemable at the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Mozambique" title="Bank of Mozambique">Bank of Mozambique</a> until the end of 2012. The US$, <a href="/wiki/South_African_rand" title="South African rand">South African rand</a>, and recently the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a> are also widely accepted and used in business transactions. The minimum legal salary is around US$60 per month. Mozambique is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a> (SADC).<sup id="cite_ref-BilateralRelationsFactSheet_13-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilateralRelationsFactSheet-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The SADC <a href="/wiki/Free_trade" title="Free trade">free trade</a> protocol is aimed at making the Southern African region more competitive by eliminating <a href="/wiki/Tariff" title="Tariff">tariffs</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Trade_barrier" title="Trade barrier">trade barriers</a>. The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> in 2007 talked of Mozambique\'s \'blistering pace of economic growth\'. A joint donor-government study in early 2007 said \'Mozambique is generally considered an aid success story.\' The <a href="/wiki/IMF" class="mw-redirect" title="IMF">IMF</a> in early 2007 said \'Mozambique is a success story in Sub-Saharan Africa.\' Yet, despite this apparent success, both the World Bank and <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a> used the word \'paradox\' to describe rising chronic <a href="/wiki/Child_malnutrition" class="mw-redirect" title="Child malnutrition">child malnutrition</a> in the face of GDP growth. Between 1994 and 2006, average annual GDP growth was approximately 8%, however, the country remains one of the poorest and most underdeveloped in the world. In a 2006 survey, three-quarters of Mozambicans said that in the past five years their economic position had remained the same or become worse.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rebounding_growth">Rebounding growth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Rebounding growth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozambique_-_traditional_sailboat.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Mozambique_-_traditional_sailboat.jpg/220px-Mozambique_-_traditional_sailboat.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Mozambique_-_traditional_sailboat.jpg/330px-Mozambique_-_traditional_sailboat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Mozambique_-_traditional_sailboat.jpg/440px-Mozambique_-_traditional_sailboat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1089" data-file-height="720" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozambique_-_traditional_sailboat.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Traditional sailboat in <a href="/wiki/Ilha_de_Mo%C3%A7ambique" class="mw-redirect" title="Ilha de Mo\xc3\xa7ambique">Ilha de Mo\xc3\xa7ambique</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Maputo_from_the_CFM_building_-_Maputo_do_predio_do_CFM_-_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Maputo_from_the_CFM_building_-_Maputo_do_predio_do_CFM_-_2.jpg/220px-Maputo_from_the_CFM_building_-_Maputo_do_predio_do_CFM_-_2.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Maputo_from_the_CFM_building_-_Maputo_do_predio_do_CFM_-_2.jpg/330px-Maputo_from_the_CFM_building_-_Maputo_do_predio_do_CFM_-_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Maputo_from_the_CFM_building_-_Maputo_do_predio_do_CFM_-_2.jpg/440px-Maputo_from_the_CFM_building_-_Maputo_do_predio_do_CFM_-_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Maputo_from_the_CFM_building_-_Maputo_do_predio_do_CFM_-_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Maputo, the capital, is the richest city of Mozambique.</div></div></div>\n<p>The resettlement of <a href="/wiki/Mozambican_Civil_War" title="Mozambican Civil War">civil war</a> <a href="/wiki/War_refugee" class="mw-redirect" title="War refugee">refugees</a> and successful economic reform have led to a high growth rate: the country enjoyed a remarkable recovery, achieving an average annual rate of economic growth of 8% between 1996 and 2006<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> and between 6\xe2\x80\x937% from 2006 to 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-databank.worldbank.org_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-databank.worldbank.org-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The devastating <a href="/wiki/2000_Mozambique_flood" title="2000 Mozambique flood">floods of early 2000</a> slowed GDP growth to 2.1%,<sup id="cite_ref-BilateralRelationsFactSheet_13-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilateralRelationsFactSheet-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> but a full recovery was achieved in 2001 with growth of 14.8%.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>. Rapid expansion in the future hinged on several major foreign investment projects, continued economic reform, and the revival of the agriculture, transportation, and tourism sectors.<sup id="cite_ref-BilateralRelationsFactSheet_13-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilateralRelationsFactSheet-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> In 2013 about 80% of the population was employed in agriculture, the majority of whom were engaged in small-scale subsistence farming<sup id="cite_ref-Canada_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canada-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> which still suffered from inadequate infrastructure, commercial networks, and investment.<sup id="cite_ref-BilateralRelationsFactSheet_13-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilateralRelationsFactSheet-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> However, in 2012, more than 90% of Mozambique\'s arable land was still <a href="/wiki/Tillage" title="Tillage">uncultivated</a>.\n</p><p>In 2013, a BBC article reported that, starting in 2009, Portuguese had been returning to Mozambique because of the growing economy in Mozambique and the poor economic situation in Portugal.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_reforms">Economic reforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Economic reforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>More than 1,200 mostly small <a href="/wiki/Nationalization" title="Nationalization">state-owned enterprises</a> have been <a href="/wiki/Privatised" class="mw-redirect" title="Privatised">privatised</a>. Preparations for privatisation and/or sector liberalisation were made for the remaining parastatal enterprises, including telecommunications, energy, ports, and railways. The government frequently selected a strategic foreign investor when privatising a parastatal. Additionally, customs duties have been reduced, and customs management has been streamlined and reformed. The government introduced a value-added tax in 1999 as part of its efforts to increase domestic revenues. Plans for 2003\xe2\x80\x9304 included Commercial Code reform; comprehensive judicial reform; financial sector strengthening; continued civil service reform; and improved government budget, audit, and inspection capability.<sup id="cite_ref-BilateralRelationsFactSheet_13-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilateralRelationsFactSheet-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Further political instability resulting from flooding left thousands homeless, displaced within their own country.<sup id="cite_ref-BilateralRelationsFactSheet_13-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilateralRelationsFactSheet-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Corruption">Corruption</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Corruption">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Mozambique\'s economy has been shaken by a number of corruption scandals. In July 2011, the government proposed new anti-corruption laws to criminalise embezzlement, influence peddling and graft, following numerous instances of the theft of public money. This has been endorsed by the country\'s Council of Ministers. Mozambique has convicted two former ministers for graft in the past two years.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Mozambique was ranked 116 of 178 countries in anti-graft watchdog <a href="/wiki/Transparency_International" title="Transparency International">Transparency International</a>\'s latest index of global corruption. According to a USAID report written in 2005, "the scale and scope of corruption in Mozambique are cause for alarm."<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In March 2012, the government of the southern Mozambican province of Inhambane uncovered the misappropriation of public funds by the director of the Provincial Anti-Drugs Office, Calisto Alberto Tomo. He was found to have colluded with the accountant in the Anti-Drugs Office, Recalda Guambe, to steal over 260,000 meticais between 2008 and 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The government of Mozambique has taken steps to address the problem of corruption, and some positive developments can be observed, such as the passages of several new anti-corruption bills in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_resources">Natural resources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Natural resources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mineral_industry_of_Mozambique" title="Mineral industry of Mozambique">Mineral industry of Mozambique</a></div>\n<p>In 2012, large natural gas reserves were discovered in Mozambique, revenues which have the potential to dramatically change the economy.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:La_plage_aux_dunes_de_Dovela_-_2012-04-28_-_75154574.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/La_plage_aux_dunes_de_Dovela_-_2012-04-28_-_75154574.jpg/220px-La_plage_aux_dunes_de_Dovela_-_2012-04-28_-_75154574.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/La_plage_aux_dunes_de_Dovela_-_2012-04-28_-_75154574.jpg/330px-La_plage_aux_dunes_de_Dovela_-_2012-04-28_-_75154574.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/La_plage_aux_dunes_de_Dovela_-_2012-04-28_-_75154574.jpg/440px-La_plage_aux_dunes_de_Dovela_-_2012-04-28_-_75154574.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="427" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:La_plage_aux_dunes_de_Dovela_-_2012-04-28_-_75154574.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a> tourists on the beach, in <a href="/wiki/Inhambane_Province" title="Inhambane Province">Inhambane</a>, Mozambique</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Mozambique" title="Tourism in Mozambique">Tourism in Mozambique</a></div>\n<p>Mozambique attracts tourists. The country\'s natural environment, wildlife, and historic heritage provide opportunities for beach, cultural, and <a href="/wiki/Eco-tourism" class="mw-redirect" title="Eco-tourism">eco-tourism</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Mozambique has a great potential for growth in its <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> (GDP),<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> although its current contribution is only 5.6%.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The beaches with clean water are suitable for tourism,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="The material near this tag possibly contains original research. (July 2018)">original research?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> especially those that are very far from urban centers, such as those in the province of <a href="/wiki/Cabo_Delgado_Province" title="Cabo Delgado Province">Cabo Delgado</a>, especially the Quirimbas Islands, and the province of <a href="/wiki/Inhambane" title="Inhambane">Inhambane</a>, especially the Archipelago of Bazaruto.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The country also has several national parks, including <a href="/wiki/Gorongosa_National_Park" title="Gorongosa National Park">Gorongosa National Park</a>, with its infrastructures rehabilitated and repopulated in certain species of animals that were already disappearing.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Mozambique" title="Transport in Mozambique">Transport in Mozambique</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Steam_locomotive_Inhambane.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Steam_locomotive_Inhambane.jpg/220px-Steam_locomotive_Inhambane.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Steam_locomotive_Inhambane.jpg/330px-Steam_locomotive_Inhambane.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Steam_locomotive_Inhambane.jpg/440px-Steam_locomotive_Inhambane.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2929" data-file-height="1947" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Steam_locomotive_Inhambane.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Steam locomotive at Inhambane, 2009.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LAM_Boeing_737-200Adv_C9-BAK_JNB_2005-12-2.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/LAM_Boeing_737-200Adv_C9-BAK_JNB_2005-12-2.png/220px-LAM_Boeing_737-200Adv_C9-BAK_JNB_2005-12-2.png" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/LAM_Boeing_737-200Adv_C9-BAK_JNB_2005-12-2.png/330px-LAM_Boeing_737-200Adv_C9-BAK_JNB_2005-12-2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/LAM_Boeing_737-200Adv_C9-BAK_JNB_2005-12-2.png/440px-LAM_Boeing_737-200Adv_C9-BAK_JNB_2005-12-2.png 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="682" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LAM_Boeing_737-200Adv_C9-BAK_JNB_2005-12-2.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>National Mozambican airline, <a href="/wiki/LAM_Mozambique_Airlines" title="LAM Mozambique Airlines">LAM Mozambique</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Modes of <a href="/wiki/Transport" title="Transport">transport</a> in Mozambique include <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport" title="Rail transport">rail</a>, <a href="/wiki/Road_transport" title="Road transport">road</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_transport" class="mw-redirect" title="Water transport">water</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Air_transport" class="mw-redirect" title="Air transport">air</a>. \n</p><p>There are over 30,000&#160;km of roads, but much of the network is unpaved. Like its <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a> neighbours, <a href="/wiki/Left-_and_right-hand_traffic" title="Left- and right-hand traffic">traffic circulates on the left</a>.\n</p><p>There is an  international <a href="/wiki/Airport" title="Airport">airport</a> at <a href="/wiki/Maputo_International_Airport" title="Maputo International Airport">Maputo</a>, 21 other paved airports, and over 100 airstrips with unpaved runways.\n</p><p>On the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a> coast are several large <a href="/wiki/Seaport" class="mw-redirect" title="Seaport">seaports</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Nacala" title="Nacala">Nacala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beira_(Mozambique)" class="mw-redirect" title="Beira (Mozambique)">Beira</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maputo" title="Maputo">Maputo</a>, with further ports being developed. There are 3,750&#160;km of <a href="/wiki/Navigability" title="Navigability">navigable</a> inland waterways. \nThere are rail links serving principal cities and connecting the country with <a href="/wiki/Malawi" title="Malawi">Malawi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>. \nThe Mozambican railway system developed over more than a century from three different ports on the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a> that served as terminals for separate lines to the hinterland.  The railroads were major targets during the <a href="/wiki/Mozambican_Civil_War" title="Mozambican Civil War">Mozambican Civil War</a>, were sabotaged by <a href="/wiki/RENAMO" title="RENAMO">RENAMO</a>, and are being rehabilitated. A <a href="/wiki/Parastatal" class="mw-redirect" title="Parastatal">parastatal</a> authority, <i>Portos e Caminhos de Ferro de Mo\xc3\xa7ambique</i> (abbreviated CFM; in English <b>Mozambique Ports and Railways</b>), oversees the railway system of Mozambique and its connected ports, but management has been largely outsourced.  Each line has its own development corridor.\n</p><p>As of  2005<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> there were 3,123&#160;km of railway track, consisting of 2,983&#160;km of <span class="nowrap">1,067&#160;mm</span> (<span class="nowrap">3&#160;ft&#160;6&#160;in</span>) gauge, compatible with neighbouring rail systems, and a 140&#160;km line of <span class="nowrap">762&#160;mm</span> (<span class="nowrap">2&#160;ft&#160;6&#160;in</span>) gauge, the <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Railway" title="Gaza Railway">Gaza Railway</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The central <a href="/wiki/Beira_Railroad_Corporation" title="Beira Railroad Corporation">Beira Railroad Corporation</a> route links the port of <a href="/wiki/Beira,_Mozambique" title="Beira, Mozambique">Beira</a> to the landlocked countries of Malawi, Zambia and Zimbabwe. To the north of this the port of <a href="/wiki/Nacala" title="Nacala">Nacala</a> is also linked by rail to Malawi, and to the south <a href="/wiki/Maputo" title="Maputo">Maputo</a> is linked to Zimbabwe and South Africa. These networks interconnect only via neighbouring countries. A new route for coal haulage between <a href="/wiki/Tete" class="mw-redirect" title="Tete">Tete</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beira,_Mozambique" title="Beira, Mozambique">Beira</a> was planned to come into service by 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> and in August 2010, Mozambique and <a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">Botswana</a> signed a memorandum of understanding to develop a 1,100&#160;km railway through Zimbabwe, to carry coal from <a href="/wiki/Serule" title="Serule">Serule</a> in Botswana to a deepwater port at <a href="/wiki/Techobanine" title="Techobanine">Techobanine</a> Point in Mozambique.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Newer rolling stock has been supplied by the Indian <a href="/wiki/Golden_Rock_Railway_Workshop" title="Golden Rock Railway Workshop">Golden Rock</a> workshop<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> using <a href="/wiki/Centre_Buffer_Coupler" class="mw-redirect" title="Centre Buffer Coupler">Centre Buffer Couplers</a> (AAR)<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Railway_air_brake" title="Railway air brake">air brakes</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply_and_sanitation">Water supply and sanitation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Water supply and sanitation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Mozambique" title="Water supply and sanitation in Mozambique">Water supply and sanitation in Mozambique</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Daily_struggle_for_water_(5400691444).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Daily_struggle_for_water_%285400691444%29.jpg/220px-Daily_struggle_for_water_%285400691444%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Daily_struggle_for_water_%285400691444%29.jpg/330px-Daily_struggle_for_water_%285400691444%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Daily_struggle_for_water_%285400691444%29.jpg/440px-Daily_struggle_for_water_%285400691444%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Daily_struggle_for_water_(5400691444).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Woman fetching water during the dry season from a polluted source in Machaze District of the Central Manica Province.</div></div></div>\n<p>Water supply and sanitation in Mozambique is characterised by low levels of access to an <a href="/wiki/Improved_water_source" title="Improved water source">improved water source</a>\n(estimated to be 51% in 2011), low levels of access to adequate\nsanitation (estimated to be 25% in 2011) and mostly poor service\nquality. In 2007 the government has defined a strategy for water supply\nand sanitation in rural areas, where 62% of the population lives. In\nurban areas, water is supplied by informal small-scale providers and by\nformal providers.\n</p><p>Beginning in 1998, Mozambique has reformed the formal part\nof the urban water supply sector through the creation of an independent\nregulatory agency called CRA, an asset-holding company called FIPAG and a\n<a href="/wiki/Public-private_partnership" class="mw-redirect" title="Public-private partnership">Public-private partnership</a>\n(PPP) with a company called Aguas de Mo\xc3\xa7ambique. The PPP covered those\nareas of the capital and of four other cities that had access to formal\nwater supply systems. However, the PPP ended when the management\ncontracts for four cities expired in 2008 and when the foreign partner\nof the company that serves the capital under a lease contract withdrew\nin 2010, claiming heavy losses.\n</p><p>While urban water supply has received considerable policy\nattention, the government has no strategy for urban sanitation yet.\nExternal donors finance about 87.4% of all public investments in the\nsector. The main donors in the water sector are the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, the <a href="/wiki/African_Development_Bank" title="African Development Bank">African Development Bank</a>, Canada, the Netherlands, Sweden, Switzerland and the United States.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Mozambique" title="Demographics of Mozambique">Demographics of Mozambique</a></div>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="4" style="text-align:center; background:#cfb;">Population in Mozambique<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="background:#cfb;">Year\n</th>\n<th style="background:#cfb;">Million\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">1950</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">6.1\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">2017</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">28.9\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">2016</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">28.8\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The north-central provinces of Zambezia and Nampula are the most populous, with about 45% of the population. The estimated four million <a href="/wiki/Macua_(people)" class="mw-redirect" title="Macua (people)">Macua</a> are the dominant group in the northern part of the country; the <a href="/wiki/Sena_people" title="Sena people">Sena</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shona_people" title="Shona people">Shona</a> (mostly <a href="/wiki/Ndau_people" title="Ndau people">Ndau</a>) are prominent in the Zambezi valley,<sup id="cite_ref-BilateralRelationsFactSheet_13-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BilateralRelationsFactSheet-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Tsonga_people" title="Tsonga people">Tsonga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soshangane" title="Soshangane">Shangaan</a> people dominate in southern Mozambique. Other groups include <a href="/wiki/Makonde_people" title="Makonde people">Makonde</a>, <a href="/wiki/WaYao" class="mw-redirect" title="WaYao">Yao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swahili_people" title="Swahili people">Swahili</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tonga_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Tonga people">Tonga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chopi_people" title="Chopi people">Chopi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nguni_people" title="Nguni people">Nguni</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Zulu_people" title="Zulu people">Zulu</a>). <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu</a> people comprise 97.8% of the population, with the rest made up of <a href="/wiki/White_Africans" class="mw-redirect" title="White Africans">White Africans</a> (largely of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Mozambicans" title="Portuguese Mozambicans">Portuguese</a> ancestry), Euro-Africans (<a href="/wiki/Creole_peoples#Africa" title="Creole peoples"><i>mesti\xc3\xa7o</i></a> people of mixed Bantu and Portuguese ancestry), and Indians.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Roughly 45,000 people of <a href="/wiki/Indians_in_Mozambique" title="Indians in Mozambique">Indian descent</a> reside in Mozambique.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During Portuguese colonial rule, a large minority of people of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> descent lived permanently in almost all areas of the country,<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> and Mozambicans with Portuguese blood at the time of independence numbered about 360,000. Many of these left the country after independence from Portugal in 1975. There are various estimates for the size of <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_Chinese_in_Mozambique" title="Ethnic Chinese in Mozambique">Mozambique\'s Chinese community</a>, ranging from 7,000 to 12,000 as of  2007<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ISN_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISN-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to a 2011 survey, the total fertility rate was 5.9 children per woman, with 6.6 in rural areas and 4.5 in urban areas.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_cities">Largest cities</span><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="navbox">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="10" class="navbox-title"><div style="float:right; width:6em; height:2.6em">&#160;</div><div style="text-align:right;"><b>100.00%</b>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mz_etnies.PNG" class="image"><img alt=""
