data-file-width="739" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mz_etnies.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ethnic map of Mozambique.</div></div></div>\n<p>Portuguese is the official and most widely spoken language of the nation, spoken by 50.3% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-knownport_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-knownport-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Most Mozambicans living in the cities speak Portuguese as their first language.\n</p><p>The Bantu-group languages of Mozambique that are indigenous to the country vary greatly in their groupings and in some cases are rather poorly appreciated and documented.<sup id="cite_ref-r1_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r1-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Apart from its lingua franca uses in the north of the country, <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili</a> is spoken in a small area of the coast next to the Tanzanian border; south of this, towards Mo\xc3\xa7ambique Island, <a href="/wiki/Kimwani" class="mw-redirect" title="Kimwani">Kimwani</a>, regarded as a dialect of Swahili, is used. Immediately inland of the Swahili area, <a href="/wiki/Makonde_language" title="Makonde language">Makonde</a> is used, separated farther inland by a small strip of <a href="/wiki/Makhuwa" class="mw-redirect" title="Makhuwa">Makhuwa</a>-speaking territory from an area where <a href="/wiki/Yao_language" title="Yao language">Yao</a> or ChiYao is used. Makonde and Yao belong to a different group, Yao<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> being very close to the <a href="/wiki/Mwera_language" title="Mwera language">Mwera language</a> of the Rondo Plateau area in Tanzania.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Prepositions appear in these languages as locative prefixes prefixed to the noun and declined according to their own noun-class. Some <a href="/wiki/Nyanja" class="mw-redirect" title="Nyanja">Nyanja</a> is used at the coast of Lake Malawi, as well as on the other side of the Lake.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Somewhat different from all of these are the languages of the eMakhuwa group, with a loss of initial k-, which means that many nouns begin with a vowel: for example, <i>epula</i> = "rain".<sup id="cite_ref-r1_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r1-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There is eMakhuwa proper, with the related <a href="/wiki/ELomwe" class="mw-redirect" title="ELomwe">eLomwe</a> and <a href="/wiki/EChuwabo" class="mw-redirect" title="EChuwabo">eChuwabo</a>, with a small <a href="/wiki/EKoti" class="mw-redirect" title="EKoti">eKoti</a>-speaking area at the coast. In an area straddling the lower Zambezi, <a href="/wiki/Sena_language" title="Sena language">Sena</a>, which belongs to the same group as Nyanja, is spoken, with areas speaking the related CiNyungwe and <a href="/wiki/CiSenga" class="mw-redirect" title="CiSenga">CiSenga</a> further upriver.\n</p><p>A large <a href="/wiki/Shona_language" title="Shona language">Shona</a>-speaking area extends between the Zimbabwe border and the sea: this was formerly known the <a href="/wiki/Ndau_people" title="Ndau people">Ndau</a> variety<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> but now uses the orthography of the Standard Shona of Zimbabwe. Apparently similar to Shona, but lacking the tone patterns of the Shona language, and regarded by its speakers as quite separate, is CiBalke, also called Rue or Barwe, used in a small country near the Zimbabwe border.\n</p><p>South of this area are languages of the <a href="/wiki/Tsonga_language" title="Tsonga language">Tsonga</a> group, which are quite different again. XiTswa or <a href="/wiki/Tswa" class="mw-redirect" title="Tswa">Tswa</a> occurs at the coast and inland, XiTsonga or <a href="/wiki/Tsonga_language" title="Tsonga language">Tsonga</a> straddles the area around the Limpopo River, including such local dialects as XiHlanganu, XiN\'walungu, XiBila, XiHlengwe, and XiDzonga. This language area extends into neighbouring South Africa. Still related to these, but distinct, are GiTonga and CiCopi or <a href="/wiki/Chopi_language" title="Chopi language">Chopi</a>, spoken north of the mouth of the Limpopo, and XiRonga or <a href="/wiki/Ronga" class="mw-redirect" title="Ronga">Ronga</a>, spoken in the immediate region around Maputo. The languages in this group are, judging by the short vocabularies,<sup id="cite_ref-r1_61-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r1-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> very vaguely similar to <a href="/wiki/Zulu_language" title="Zulu language">Zulu</a>, but obviously not in the same immediate group. There are small <a href="/wiki/Swazi_language" title="Swazi language">Swazi</a>- and <a href="/wiki/Zulu_language" title="Zulu language">Zulu</a>-speaking areas in Mozambique immediately next to the Swaziland and KwaZulu-Natal borders.\n</p><p>Arabs, Chinese, and Indians primarily speak Portuguese and some Hindi. Indians from Portuguese India speak any of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Creole" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese Creole">Portuguese Creoles</a> of their origin aside from Portuguese as their second language.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Mozambique" title="Religion in Mozambique">Religion in Mozambique</a></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:194px;max-width:194px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:192px;max-width:192px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:S%C3%A9_da_Beira.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/S%C3%A9_da_Beira.jpg/190px-S%C3%A9_da_Beira.jpg" width="190" height="285" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/S%C3%A9_da_Beira.jpg/285px-S%C3%A9_da_Beira.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/S%C3%A9_da_Beira.jpg/380px-S%C3%A9_da_Beira.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1843" data-file-height="2764" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Beira Cathedral</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:192px;max-width:192px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Mesquita_Maputo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Mesquita_Maputo.jpg/190px-Mesquita_Maputo.jpg" width="190" height="143" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Mesquita_Maputo.jpg/285px-Mesquita_Maputo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Mesquita_Maputo.jpg/380px-Mesquita_Maputo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">A mosque in downtown Maputo</div></div></div></div>\n<p>The 2007 census found that Christians made up 56.1% of Mozambique\'s population and Muslims comprised 17.9% of the population. 7.3% of the people held other beliefs, mainly <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">animism</a>, and 18.7% had no religious beliefs.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> A more recent government survey conducted by the <a href="/wiki/Demographic_and_Health_Surveys" title="Demographic and Health Surveys">Demographic and Health Surveys</a> Program in 2015 indicated that Catholicism had increased to 30.5% of the population, Muslims constituted 19.3%, and various Protestant groups a total of 44%.<sup id="cite_ref-DHS_2015_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DHS_2015-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Roman Catholic Church has established twelve dioceses (Beira, Chimoio, Guru\xc3\xa9, Inhambane, Lichinga, Maputo, Nacala, Nampula, Pemba, Quelimane, Tete,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> and Xai-Xai; archdioceses are <a href="/wiki/Beira,_Mozambique" title="Beira, Mozambique">Beira</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maputo" title="Maputo">Maputo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nampula" title="Nampula">Nampula</a>). Statistics for the dioceses range from a low 5.8% Catholics in the population in the diocese of Chimoio, to 32.50% in Quelimane diocese (Anuario catolico de Mocambique 2007).\n</p><p>The work of Methodism in Mozambique started in 1890. The Rev. Dr. Erwin Richards began a Methodist mission at Chicuque in Inhambane Province. A Igreja Metodista Unida em Mo\xc3\xa7ambique (the UMC in Mozambique) observed the 100th anniversary of Methodist presence in Mozambique in 1990. Then-Mozambique President Chissano praised the work and role of the UMC to more than 10,000 people who attended the ceremony.\n</p><p>The United Methodist Church has tripled in size in Mozambique since 1998. There are now more than 150,000 members in more than 180 congregations of the 24 districts. New pastors are ordained each year. New churches are chartered each year in each Annual Conference (North and South).<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> (LDS Church) has established a growing presence in Mozambique. It first began sending missionaries to Mozambique in 1999, and, as of April 2015, has more than 7,943 members.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bah\xc3\xa1&#39;\xc3\xad Faith">Bah\xc3\xa1\'\xc3\xad Faith</a> has been present in Mozambique since the early 1950s but did not openly identify itself in those years because of the strong influence of the Catholic Church which did not recognise it officially as a world religion. The independence in 1975 saw the entrance of new pioneers. In total there are about 3,000 declared Baha\'is in Mozambique as of  2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>. The Administrative Committee is located in Maputo.\n</p><p>Muslims are particularly present in the north of the country. They are organised in several "<a href="/wiki/Tariqa" title="Tariqa">tariqa</a>" or <a href="/wiki/Fraternity" title="Fraternity">brotherhoods</a>. Two national organisations also exist\xe2\x80\x94the <i>Conselho Isl\xc3\xa2mico de Mo\xc3\xa7ambique</i> and the <i>Congresso Isl\xc3\xa2mico de Mo\xc3\xa7ambique</i>. There are also important Pakistani, Indian associations as well as some Shia communities.\n</p><p>Among the main <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> churches are <a href="/wiki/Igreja_Uni%C3%A3o_Baptista_de_Mo%C3%A7ambique" title="Igreja Uni\xc3\xa3o Baptista de Mo\xc3\xa7ambique">Igreja Uni\xc3\xa3o Baptista de Mo\xc3\xa7ambique</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Assembleias_de_Deus" title="Assembleias de Deus">Assembleias de Deus</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventists" class="mw-redirect" title="Seventh-day Adventists">Seventh-day Adventists</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Church_of_Southern_Africa" title="Anglican Church of Southern Africa">Anglican Church of Southern Africa</a>, the Igreja do Evangelho Completo de Deus, the <a href="/wiki/Igreja_Metodista_Unida" title="Igreja Metodista Unida">Igreja Metodista Unida</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Igreja_Presbiteriana_de_Mo%C3%A7ambique" title="Igreja Presbiteriana de Mo\xc3\xa7ambique">Igreja Presbiteriana de Mo\xc3\xa7ambique</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Igrejas_de_Cristo" title="Igrejas de Cristo">Igrejas de Cristo</a> and the Assembleia Evang\xc3\xa9lica de Deus.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Mozambique" title="Health in Mozambique">Health in Mozambique</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Mosambik_2016.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Mosambik_2016.png/220px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Mosambik_2016.png" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Mosambik_2016.png/330px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Mosambik_2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Mosambik_2016.png/440px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Mosambik_2016.png 2x" data-file-width="610" data-file-height="425" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Mosambik_2016.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Population pyramid 2016</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Luabo_hospital_(4754619071).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Luabo_hospital_%284754619071%29.jpg/220px-Luabo_hospital_%284754619071%29.jpg" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Luabo_hospital_%284754619071%29.jpg/330px-Luabo_hospital_%284754619071%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Luabo_hospital_%284754619071%29.jpg/440px-Luabo_hospital_%284754619071%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="605" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Luabo_hospital_(4754619071).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hospital in Luabo</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Number_of_patients_on_Anti_Retroviral_Treatment_in_Mozambique_2003-2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Number_of_patients_on_Anti_Retroviral_Treatment_in_Mozambique_2003-2011.jpg/220px-Number_of_patients_on_Anti_Retroviral_Treatment_in_Mozambique_2003-2011.jpg" width="220" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Number_of_patients_on_Anti_Retroviral_Treatment_in_Mozambique_2003-2011.jpg/330px-Number_of_patients_on_Anti_Retroviral_Treatment_in_Mozambique_2003-2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Number_of_patients_on_Anti_Retroviral_Treatment_in_Mozambique_2003-2011.jpg/440px-Number_of_patients_on_Anti_Retroviral_Treatment_in_Mozambique_2003-2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1072" data-file-height="653" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Number_of_patients_on_Anti_Retroviral_Treatment_in_Mozambique_2003-2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The increase in number of HIV positive Mozambicans on <a href="/wiki/Antiretroviral_drug" class="mw-redirect" title="Antiretroviral drug">Antiretroviral treatment</a>, 2003\xe2\x80\x9314</div></div></div>\n<p>The fertility rate is at about 5.5 births per woman. Public expenditure on health was at 2.7% of the GDP in 2004, whereas private expenditure on health was at 1.3% in the same year. Health expenditure per capita was 42 US$ (PPP) in 2004. In the early 21st century there were 3 physicians per 100,000 people in the country. <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality" title="Infant mortality">Infant mortality</a> was at 100 per 1,000 births in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After its independence from Portugal in 1975, the Mozambique government established a primary health care system that was cited by the WHO as a model for other developing countries.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Over 90% of the population had been provided with vaccination. During the period of the early 1980s, around 11% of the government budget was targeted on health care.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The Mozambique civil war led to a great setback in the primary health system in Mozambique. The RENAMO\'s attack on government infrastructures included health and education systems from 1980 to 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-Pfeiffer._J._2003_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pfeiffer._J._2003-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 2010 maternal mortality rate per 100,000 births for Mozambique is 550. This is compared with 598.8 in 2008 and 385 in 1990. The under 5 mortality rate, per 1,000 births is 147 and the neonatal mortality as a percentage of under 5s mortality is 29. In Mozambique the number of midwives per 1,000 live births is 3 and the lifetime risk of death for pregnant women 1 in 37.<sup id="cite_ref-SOWMY_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SOWMY-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The official HIV <a href="/wiki/Prevalence" title="Prevalence">prevalence</a> in Mozambique in 2011 was 11.5% of the population aged between 15 and 49 years. In the southern parts of Mozambique\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/Maputo_Province" title="Maputo Province">Maputo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Province" title="Gaza Province">Gaza</a> provinces as well as the city of Maputo\xe2\x80\x94the official figures are more than twice as high as the national average. In 2011 the health authorities estimated about 1.7 million Mozambicans were HIV-positive, of whom 600,000 were in need of anti-retroviral treatment. As of December 2011, 240,000 were receiving such treatment, increasing to 416,000 in March 2014 according to the health authorities. According to the 2011 UNAIDS Report, the HIV/AIDS epidemic in Mozambique seems to be levelling off.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Mozambique" title="Education in Mozambique">Education in Mozambique</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozambique_school.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Mozambique_school.jpg/170px-Mozambique_school.jpg" width="170" height="82" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Mozambique_school.jpg/255px-Mozambique_school.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Mozambique_school.jpg/340px-Mozambique_school.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2031" data-file-height="984" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozambique_school.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pupils in front of their school in <a href="/wiki/Nampula" title="Nampula">Nampula</a>, Mozambique</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozambique_classroom.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Mozambique_classroom.jpg/170px-Mozambique_classroom.jpg" width="170" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Mozambique_classroom.jpg/255px-Mozambique_classroom.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Mozambique_classroom.jpg/340px-Mozambique_classroom.jpg 2x" data-file-width="343" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozambique_classroom.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>School children in the classroom</div></div></div>\n<p>Portuguese is the primary language of instruction in all of the Mozambican schools. All Mozambicans are required by law to attend school through the primary level; however, a lot of children in Mozambique do not go to primary school because they have to work for their families\' subsistence farms for a living. In 2007, one million children still did not go to school, most of them from poor rural families, and almost half of all teachers in Mozambique were still unqualified. Girls\xe2\x80\x99 enrollment increased from 3 million in 2002 to 4.1 million in 2006 while the completion rate increased from 31,000 to 90,000, which testified a very poor completion rate.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After grade 7, pupils must take standardised national exams to enter secondary school, which runs from eighth to 10th grade.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Space in Mozambican universities is extremely limited; thus most pupils who complete pre-university school do not immediately proceed on to university studies. Many go to work as teachers or are unemployed. There are also institutes which give more vocational training, specialising in agricultural, technical or pedagogical studies, which students may attend after grade 10 in lieu of a pre-university school.\n</p><p>After independence from Portugal in 1975, a number of Mozambican pupils continued to be admitted every year at Portuguese high schools, polytechnical institutes and universities, through bilateral agreements between the Portuguese government and the Mozambican government.\n</p><p>According to 2010 estimates, the <a href="/wiki/Literacy_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Literacy rate">literacy rate</a> of Mozambique was 56.1% (70.8% male and 42.8% female).<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> By 2015, this had increased to 58.8% (73.3% male and 45.4% female).<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozambique_-_mask.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Mozambique_-_mask.jpg/170px-Mozambique_-_mask.jpg" width="170" height="252" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Mozambique_-_mask.jpg/255px-Mozambique_-_mask.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Mozambique_-_mask.jpg/340px-Mozambique_-_mask.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="1067" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozambique_-_mask.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Woman with traditional mask in Mozambique</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Museu_Da_Ilha_De_Mocambique_(33387901932).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Museu_Da_Ilha_De_Mocambique_%2833387901932%29.jpg/220px-Museu_Da_Ilha_De_Mocambique_%2833387901932%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Museu_Da_Ilha_De_Mocambique_%2833387901932%29.jpg/330px-Museu_Da_Ilha_De_Mocambique_%2833387901932%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Museu_Da_Ilha_De_Mocambique_%2833387901932%29.jpg/440px-Museu_Da_Ilha_De_Mocambique_%2833387901932%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Museu_Da_Ilha_De_Mocambique_(33387901932).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Island_of_Mozambique" title="Island of Mozambique">Island of Mozambique</a>, 2016</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Mozambique" title="Culture of Mozambique">Culture of Mozambique</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_identity">Cultural identity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Cultural identity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Mozambique was ruled by Portugal, and they share a main language (Portuguese) and main religion (Roman Catholicism). But since most of the people of Mozambique are <a href="/wiki/Bantus" class="mw-redirect" title="Bantus">Bantus</a>, most of the culture is native; for Bantus living in urban areas, there is some Portuguese influence. Mozambican culture also influences the <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Portugal" title="Culture of Portugal">Portuguese culture</a>. Mozambican food, <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Mozambique" title="Music of Mozambique">music</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Mozambican_films" title="List of Mozambican films">movies</a> (by <a href="/wiki/RTP_%C3%81frica" title="RTP \xc3\x81frica">RTP \xc3\x81frica</a>), and traditions are now part of everyday lifestyles of Portugal.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">Arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Makonde_people" title="Makonde people">Makonde</a> are known for their wood carving and elaborate masks, that are commonly used in traditional dances. There are two different kinds of wood carvings: <a href="/wiki/Shetani" title="Shetani">shetani</a>, (evil spirits), which are mostly carved in heavy <a href="/wiki/Ebony" title="Ebony">ebony</a>, tall, and elegantly curved with symbols and nonrepresentational faces; and <a href="/wiki/Ujamaa" title="Ujamaa">ujamaa</a>, which are totem-type carvings which illustrate lifelike faces of people and various figures. These sculptures are usually referred to as "family trees", because they tell stories of many generations.\n</p><p>During the last years of the colonial period, Mozambican art reflected the oppression by the colonial power, and became symbol of the resistance. After independence in 1975, the modern art came into a new phase. The two best known and most influential contemporary Mozambican artists are the painter <a href="/wiki/Malangatana_Ngwenya" title="Malangatana Ngwenya">Malangatana Ngwenya</a> and the sculptor <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Chissano" title="Alberto Chissano">Alberto Chissano</a>. A lot of the post-independence art during the 1980s and 1990s reflect the political struggle, civil war, suffering, starvation, and struggle.\n</p><p>Dances are usually intricate, highly developed traditions throughout Mozambique. There are many different kinds of dances from tribe to tribe which are usually ritualistic in nature. The Chopi, for instance, act out battles dressed in animal skins. The men of <a href="/wiki/Makua_(people)" class="mw-redirect" title="Makua (people)">Makua</a> dress in colourful outfits and masks while dancing on stilts around the village for hours. Groups of women in the northern part of the country perform a traditional dance called <a href="/wiki/Tufo_(dance)" title="Tufo (dance)"><i>tufo</i></a>, to celebrate <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islamic</a> holidays.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_cuisine" title="Portuguese cuisine">Portuguese cuisine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Mozambique" title="Cuisine of Mozambique">Cuisine of Mozambique</a>, and <a href="/wiki/African_cuisine" title="African cuisine">African cuisine</a></div>\n<p>With a nearly 500-year presence in the country, the Portuguese have greatly influenced Mozambique\'s cuisine. Staples and crops such as <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a> (a starchy root of Brazilian origin) and <a href="/wiki/Cashew" title="Cashew">cashew</a> nuts (also of Brazilian origin, though Mozambique was once the largest producer of these nuts<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>), and <i>p\xc3\xa3ozinho</i> (pronounced <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Portuguese" title="Help:IPA/Portuguese">[p\xc9\x90\xcc\x83w\xcb\x88z\xc4\xa9\xc9\xb2u]</a></span>, Portuguese-style French buns<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>), were brought in by the Portuguese. The use of spices and <a href="/wiki/Seasoning" title="Seasoning">seasonings</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Bay_leaf" title="Bay leaf">bay leaves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chili_pepper" title="Chili pepper">chili peppers</a>, fresh <a href="/wiki/Coriander" title="Coriander">coriander</a>, garlic, onions, <a href="/wiki/Paprika" title="Paprika">paprika</a>, red sweet peppers, and wine were introduced by the Portuguese, as were maize, <a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">millet</a>, potatoes, rice, <a href="/wiki/Sorghum" title="Sorghum">sorghum</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a>. <i>espetada</i> (<a href="/wiki/Kebab" title="Kebab">kebab</a>), the popular <i>inteiro com piripiri</i> (whole chicken in <a href="/wiki/Piri-piri" class="mw-redirect" title="Piri-piri">piri-piri</a> sauce), <i>prego</i> (steak roll), <i>pudim</i> (<a href="/wiki/Pudding" title="Pudding">pudding</a>), and <i>riss\xc3\xb3is</i> (battered shrimp) are all Portuguese dishes commonly eaten in present-day Mozambique.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Mozambique" title="Media of Mozambique">Media of Mozambique</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Radio_Mo%C3%A7ambique_(4106248049).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Radio_Mo%C3%A7ambique_%284106248049%29.jpg/220px-Radio_Mo%C3%A7ambique_%284106248049%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Radio_Mo%C3%A7ambique_%284106248049%29.jpg/330px-Radio_Mo%C3%A7ambique_%284106248049%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Radio_Mo%C3%A7ambique_%284106248049%29.jpg/440px-Radio_Mo%C3%A7ambique_%284106248049%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="682" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Radio_Mo%C3%A7ambique_(4106248049).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Headquarters of R\xc3\xa1dio Mo\xc3\xa7ambique in <a href="/w/index.php?title=KaMpfumo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="KaMpfumo (page does not exist)">KaMpfumo</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;(<a href="https://ceb.wikipedia.org/wiki/KaMpfumo" class="extiw" title="ceb:KaMpfumo">ceb</a>)</span> district of <a href="/wiki/Maputo" title="Maputo">Maputo</a> (photo 2009)</div></div></div>\n<p>Mozambican media is heavily influenced by the government.<sup id="cite_ref-salgado_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-salgado-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><b>Newspapers</b> have relatively low circulation rates, due to high newspaper prices and low <a href="/wiki/Literacy_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Literacy rate">literacy rates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-salgado_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-salgado-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Among the most highly circulated newspapers are state-controlled dailies, such as <i>Noticias</i> and <i>Di\xc3\xa1rio de Mo\xc3\xa7ambique</i>, and the weekly <i>Domingo</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-eisa_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eisa-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Their circulation is mostly confined to Maputo.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Most funding and advertising revenue is given to pro-government newspapers.<sup id="cite_ref-salgado_81-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-salgado-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> However, the number of private newspapers with critical views of the government have increased significantly in recent years.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (May 2016)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-eisa_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eisa-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><b><a href="/wiki/Radio" title="Radio">Radio</a> programmes</b> are the most influential form of media in the country due to their ease of access.<sup id="cite_ref-salgado_81-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-salgado-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> State-owned radio stations are more popular than privately owned media. This is exemplified by the government radio station, R\xc3\xa1dio Mo\xc3\xa7ambique, the most popular station in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-salgado_81-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-salgado-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> It was established shortly after Mozambique\'s independence.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <b><a href="/wiki/Television" title="Television">T.V.</a></b> stations watched by Mozambicans are STV, TIM, and TVM Televis\xc3\xa3o Mo\xc3\xa7ambique. Through cable and satellite, viewers can access tens of other African, Asian, Brazilian, and European channels.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Mozambique" title="Music of Mozambique">Music of Mozambique</a></div>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small><i>(May 2016)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Mozambique" title="Music of Mozambique">music of Mozambique</a> serves many purposes, ranging from religious expression to traditional ceremonies. Musical instruments are usually handmade. Some of the instruments used in Mozambican musical expression include drums made of wood and animal skin; the <i>lupembe</i>, a woodwind instrument made from animal horns or wood; and the <a href="/wiki/Marimba" title="Marimba">marimba</a>, which is a kind of <a href="/wiki/Xylophone" title="Xylophone">xylophone</a> native to Mozambique and other parts of Africa. The marimba is a popular instrument with the <a href="/wiki/Chopi_people" title="Chopi people">Chopi</a> of the south central coast, who are famous for their musical skill and dance.\n</p><p>Some<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (January 2011)">who?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> would say that Mozambique\'s music is similar to <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">reggae</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indian</a> <a href="/wiki/Calypso_music" title="Calypso music">calypso</a>. Other music types are popular in Mozambique like <a href="/wiki/Marrabenta" title="Marrabenta">marrabenta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kwaito" title="Kwaito">kwaito</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afrobeat" title="Afrobeat">afrobeat</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Lusophone_music" title="Lusophone music">Lusophone music</a> forms like <a href="/wiki/Fado" title="Fado">fado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bossa_nova" title="Bossa nova">bossa nova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kizomba" title="Kizomba">kizomba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Semba" title="Semba">semba</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_holidays">National holidays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" Christmas\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <i lang="pt">futebol</i>) is the most popular sport in Mozambique. The national team is the <a href="/wiki/Mozambique_national_football_team" title="Mozambique national football team">Mozambique national football team</a>. <a href="/wiki/Roller_hockey_(quad)" title="Roller hockey (quad)">Roller hockey</a> is also popular and the best results for the national team was when they came fourth at the <a href="/wiki/2011_FIRS_Men%27s_Roller_Hockey_World_Cup" title="2011 FIRS Men&#39;s Roller Hockey World Cup">2011 FIRS Roller Hockey World Cup</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul of Mozambique">Outline of Mozambique</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mozambique&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 35em; -webkit-column-width: 35em; column-width: 35em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-SpL-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-SpL_1-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Neto, Oct\xc3\xa1vio Amorim; Lobo, Marina Costa (2010). "Between Constitutional Diffusion and Local Politics: Semi-Presidentialism in Portuguese-Speaking Countries". <a href="/wiki/Social_Science_Research_Network" title="Social Science Research
